Jamison Brereton

1 (235)
Agni
Vi┼Ыv─Бmitra G─Бthina
23 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh
In our interpretation, Agni opens the hymn with a declaration that the priests have kindled him to carry the oblations. The poet and the priests then confirm that they have indeed laid the fire to begin the rite. Implied in the first two verses is thus the birth of the sacrificial fire, and the birth of Agni then becomes the central theme of the hymn. The first part of the hymn (vss. 3тАУ14) reflects not only on the birth of the ritual fire, but also on AgniтАЩs ultimate birth from the waters. Indeed, throughout much of the first half of the hymn, the verses can be taken as describing either the birth of the ritual fire or the ultimate birth of Agni or both. The poem thus merges AgniтАЩs original or ultimate birth among the waters and his birth here in the sacrifice to the accompaniment of the priestly recitations. This poetic strategy complicates the translation and interpretation of the hymn. For example, verse 4 refers to the тАЬseven young women,тАЭ who are also the mares who tend to Agni (4cd) and who

reappear again in verses 6 and 9. In verse 4 these seven women are likely the riv ers, as Geldner rightly notes, but in verse 6 they are identified, unexpectedly, as the voices of the seven priests of the soma rite. Retrospectively, therefore, we can view these women as both the rivers and the voices. Similarly in verse 11 the тАЬkindred
sistersтАЭ might be the rivers, or they might again be the voices of the priests. The identity of AgniтАЩs father also complicates the story of AgniтАЩs birth. In verse 10 Agni gives rise to Agni, and therefore Agni is also his own father. But then who is the father in verse 9? Geldner and Renou think that his father there is Heaven, HeavenтАЩs udder the raincloud, and therefore the fire here is lightning. More likely, however, the reference is to the ritual fire. If so, then the father in verse 9 might be the priest churning the fire, the udder his voice, and the udderтАЩs тАЬspurts and streamsтАЭ the words of the priest. Or, again in light of verse 10, the father might be Agni, who nurtures himself through the тАЬspurts and streamsтАЭ of his spreading flames. Or, just as in the case of the тАЬseven young women,тАЭ the poet may intend several of these possibilities.
As Geldner notes, from verse 15 the poet more unambiguously addresses the ritual fire, though he does return to the theme of AgniтАЩs births in verse 20. This time, though, the reference may be not only to the ultimate origins of Agni but also and primarily to the ritual fires of long ago and the ritual fire of the present.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬRender me vigorous, Agni, since you have made me the bearer of the Soma to offer it in the sacrifice; honouring the gods who are present, I take hold of the stone (to express Soma); I propitiate them; do you, Agni, protect my person n.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Vi┼Ыv─Бmitra was a kс╣гatriya, of royal or military profession, and was also a monarch for some time; he descended from Ku┼Ыa or the lunar lineage and was the ancestor of many royal and saintly person ns, who, like himself, were called after their common ancestor, Ku┼Ыikas, or Kau┼Ыikas. By the force of his austerities, he compelled Brahm─Б to admit into the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa order. He sought this position to be equated with Vasiс╣гс╣нha, which whom he had disputed earlier. The circumstances of his dispute with Vasiс╣гс╣нha are detailed in the R─Бm─Бyaс╣Зa; the legend is also told in the Mah─Бbh─Бrata, V─Бyu, Viс╣гс╣Зu and Bh─Бgavata Pur─Бс╣Зas. Vi┼Ыv─Бmitra and Vasiс╣гс╣нha had the patronage of hostile princes; but both had friendly relations with the royal family of Ayodhy─Б, or King Da┼Ыaratha and his son, R─Бma

Jamison Brereton

[Agni:] тАЬYou have made me your draft-horse, who am mighty from somaтАФ(saying,) тАШConvey (the oblations), o AgniтАЩтАФin order (for me) to offer the sacrifice at the ritual distribution.тАЭ
[The poet:] тАЬAs you shine toward the godsтАФI harness the stone and

Griffith

THOU, Agni, who wilt have the strong, hast made me the Soma’s priest, to worship in assembly.
Thou shinest to the Gods, I set the pressstones. I toil; be joyful in thyself, O Agni.

Oldenberg

Thou wilt have me, O Agni, as a strong (master) of Soma 1: therefore thou hast made me the carrier (of the gods?) to perform worship at the sacrifice 2. Sending my thoughts to the gods 3 I make the (press-) stone ready 4; I toil, O Agni: find thou pleasure in thy own body 5.

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЗрд╕ рдордиреНрддреНрд░ рдореЗрдВ рд╡рд╛рдЪрдХрд▓реБрдкреНрддреЛрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдЩреНрдХрд╛рд░ рд╣реИред рдЬреЛ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдп рдРрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдп рдХреЗ рдХрд░рдиреЗ рдХреА рдЗрдЪреНрдЫрд╛ рдХрд░реЗрдВ, рд╡реЗ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреЛрдВ рдХреА рд╕рдВрдЧрддрд┐ рд╕реЗ рд╢рд░реАрд░ рдХреЛ рдиреАрд░реЛрдЧ рд░рдЦрдХрд░ рдЕрдкрдиреЗ рдХреЛ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдмрдирд╛ рдХреЗ рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐ рдЖрджрд┐ рдХреА рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛ рд╕реЗ рдХрд╛рд░реНрдпреНрдпреЛрдВ рдХреЛ рд╕рд┐рджреНрдз рдХрд░реЗрдВ реерезрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рдЕрдЧреНрдиреЗ ! рдпрд╕реНрддреНрд╡рдВ рд╕реЛрдорд╕реНрдп рддрд╡рд╕рдВ рдорд╛ рд╡рд╣реНрдирд┐рдВ рд╡рдХреНрд╖рд┐ рд╡рд┐рджрдереЗ рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдпрдЬрдзреНрдпреИ рдЕрдЪреНрдЫ рдЪрдХрд░реНрде рддреЗрди рд╕рд╣рд╛рд╣рдВ рджреАрджреНрдпрддреНрд╕рдиреН рд╡рд┐рджрдереЗ рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдпрдЬрдзреНрдпреИ рдпреБрдЮреНрдЬреЗ рдпрдерд╛рд╜рдЧреНрдирд┐рд░рджреНрд░рд┐рдВ рд╡рд╣рддрд┐ рддрдерд╛рд╜рд╣рдВ рд╡рд┐рджреБрд╖рд╛рдВ рд╕рдореАрдкреЗ рд╢рдорд╛рдпреЗред рд╣реЗ рдЕрдЧреНрдиреЗ ! рд╢рд┐рд╖реНрдпреЛ рдпрдерд╛ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рдЪреНрдЫрд░реАрд░рдВ рд╕реЗрд╡рддреЗ рддрдерд╛ рдЪ рддрдиреНрд╡рдВ рдЬреБрд╖рд╕реНрд╡реерезрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдЕрде рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рджреНрдЧреБрдгрд╛рдирд╛рд╣ред

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рд╕реЛрдорд╕реНрдп) рдРрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдпрд╕реНрдп рд╕рдХрд╛рд╢рд╛рддреН (рдорд╛) рдорд╛рдореН (рддрд╡рд╕рдореН) рдмрд▓рдпреБрдХреНрддрдореН (рд╡рдХреНрд╖рд┐) рд╡рджрд╕рд┐ (рдЕрдЧреНрдиреЗ) рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рдиреН (рд╡рд╣реНрдирд┐рдореН) рд╡рд╛рд╣рдХрдВ рдкрд╛рд╡рдХрдореН (рдЪрдХрд░реНрде) рдХрд░реЛрд╖рд┐ (рд╡рд┐рджрдереЗ) рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рддреНрд╕рддреНрдХрд╛рд░рд╛рдЦреНрдпреЗ рдпрдЬреНрдЮреЗ (рдпрдЬрдзреНрдпреИ) рдпрд╖реНрдЯреБрдВ рд╕рдВрдЧрдиреНрддреБрдВ (рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдиреН) рд╡рд┐рджреБрд╖реЛ рджрд┐рд╡реНрдпрдЧреБрдгрд╛рдиреН рд╡рд╛ (рдЕрдЪреНрдЫ) рд╕рдореНрдпрдХреНред рдЕрддреНрд░ рдирд┐рдкрд╛рддрд╕реНрдп рдЪреЗрддрд┐ рджреАрд░реНрдШрдГред (рджреАрджреНрдпрддреН) рджреЗрджреАрдкреНрдпрдорд╛рдирдГ (рдпреБрдЮреНрдЬреЗ) (рдЕрджреНрд░рд┐рдореН) рдореЗрдШрдореН (рд╢рдорд╛рдпреЗ) рд╢рдордорд┐рд╡рд╛рдЪрд░рд╛рдорд┐ (рдЕрдЧреНрдиреЗ) рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рд╡рджреНрд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрдорд╛рди (рддрдиреНрд╡рдореН) (рдЬреБрд╖рд╕реНрд╡) реерезрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЕрддреНрд░ рд╡рд╛рдЪрдХрд▓реБрдкреНрддреЛрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдЩреНрдХрд╛рд░рдГред рдпреЗ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛ рдРрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдпреНрдпрдВ рдЪрд┐рдХреАрд░реНрд╖реЗрдпреБрд╕реНрддреЗ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рддреНрд╕рдВрдЧрддреНрдпрд╛ рд╢рд░реАрд░рдорд░реЛрдЧрдВ рд╕рдВрд░рдХреНрд╖реНрдпрд╛рддреНрдорд╛рдирдВ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдВрд╕рдВ рд╕рдореНрдкрд╛рджреНрдпрд╛рдЧреНрдиреНрдпрд╛рджрд┐рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрдпрд╛ рдХрд╛рд░реНрдпреНрдпрд╛рдгрд┐ рд╕рд╛рдзрдпреЗрдпреБрдГ реерезрее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдпрд╛ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рдд рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рди, рд╕реНрддреНрд░реА-рдкреБрд░реБрд╖ рд╡ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛, рдЬрдиреНрдорд╛рдЪреА рдкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕рд╛ рдЕрд╕рд▓реНрдпрд╛рдореБрд│реЗ рдпрд╛ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рдЪреНрдпрд╛ рдЕрд░реНрдерд╛рдЪреА рдорд╛рдЧреАрд▓ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдмрд░реЛрдмрд░ рд╕рдВрдЧрддреА рдЖрд╣реЗ, рд╣реЗ рдЬрд╛рдгрд╛рд╡реЗ.

рд╣реЗрдЕрдЧреНрдиреЗ рд╡рдпрдВ рдпрдЬреНрдЮрдВ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдЮреНрдЪрдВ рдкреНрд░рдХрд░реНрд╖реЗрдгрдЧреНрдЪреНрдЫрдиреНрддрдВ рдЪрдХреГрдо рдЕрдХрд╛рд░реНрд╖реНрдо рдЧреАрдГ рдорджреАрдпрд╛рд╕реНрддреБрддрд┐рдГ рд╡рд░реНрдзрддрд╛рдВ рдПрдзрддрд╛рдВ рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рдВрд╕рдорд┐рджреНрдзрд┐рд░реНрдирдореНрд╕реНрд╡рд╛рд╣рд╡рд┐рд╖рд╛рдЪрджреБрд╡рд╕реНрдпрдиреН рдЕрд╕реНрдореНрджреАрдпрд╛рдГ рдкрд░рд┐рдЪрд░реЗрдпреБрдГ рдХрд┐рдЮреНрдЪ рджрд┐рд╡реЛрджреНрдпреБрд▓реЛрдХрд╛рджрд╛рдЧрддреНрдп рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдГ рдХрд╡реАрдирд╛рдВ рд╕реНрддреЛрддреДрдгрд╛рдВ рд╡рд┐рджрдерд╛ рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирд╛рдирд┐ рд╕реНрддреЛрддреНрд░рд╛рдгрд┐рд╡рд╛рд╢рд╢рд╛рд╕реБрдГ рдЕрдиреНрд╡рд╢рд┐рд╖рдиреН рдЕрдкрд┐рдЪ рдЧреГрддреНрд╕рд╛рдп рдЧреГрдгрд╛рддреЗрд░рд┐рджрдВ рд░реВрдкрдВ рд╕реНрддреЛрддрд╡реНрдпрд╛рдпрд╛рдЧреНрдирдпреЗ рддрд╡рд╕реЗрд╡реГрджреНрдзрд╛рдп рдЧрд╛рддреБрдВрд╕реНрддреЛрддреБрдВ рдИрд╖реБрд╢реНрд░рд┐рддреН рд╕реНрддреЛрддрд╛рд░рдЗрдЪреНрдЫрдиреНрддрд┐рдЪ рдЪрд┐рджрд┐рддрд┐рдЪрд╛рд░реНрдереЗ рее реи рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWe have performed, Agni, a successful sacrifice; may my praise magnify (you) as worshipping you with fuel and with reverence; (the gods) fromheaven desire the adoration of the pious, who are anxious to praise the adorable and mighty (Agni).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

[The priests:] тАЬWe have made the sacrifice turned to the east (in order to begin). Let our song become strong.тАЭ (So saying) they befriend Agni with kindling wood and with reverence.
From heaven they [=the gods?] have directed the ritual distributions of the sages. They have sought the way for (Agni), even for the clever and mighty one.

Griffith

East have we turned the rite; may the hymn aid it. With wood and worship shall they honour Agni.
From heaven the synods of the wise have learnt it: c’en for the quick and strong they seek advancement.

Oldenberg

1 Eastward we have turned the sacrifice 2; may the prayer increase. They honoured Agni with fuel and adoration. They have taught (him) the sacrificial ordinances of the sages of Heaven 3. Though he (Agni) is clever and strong, they have sought a way for him.

Geldner

Wir haben das Opfer vorgef├╝hrt, das Lied soll wachsen. Mit Brennh├╢lzern und Verneigung bevorzugten sie den Agni. Des Himmels Seher haben die weisen Reden der Seher angeleitet. Sie suchten f├╝r ihn, der schon selbst erfahren und stark ist, einen Weg.

Grassmann

Wir f├╢rderten das Opfer, Sang gedeihe; Agni versahn mit Flammen sie voll Ehrfurcht, Vom Himmel lehrten sie die Schar der Priester und schafften Fortgang jedem raschen, starken.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe gods discovered the graceful Agni (concealed) amidst the waters of the flowing (rivers), for the purpose of (sacred) acts; Agni, who is intelligent,of purified vigour, and friendly; who from his birth bestowed happiness on earth and heaven.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The wise (Agni) of refined skill created joy for himselfтАФhe who through his birth is the close kin of heaven and of earth.
The gods found the lovely one within the waters; (they found) Agni in the work of the sisters [=rivers or fingers of the priests].

Griffith

The Prudent, he whose will is pure, brought welfare, allied by birth to Heaven and Earth in kinship.
The Gods discovered in the midst of waters beautiful Agni with the Sisters’ labour.

Oldenberg

He has conceived freshness 1, the wise one of pure 2 powers, he who is by his birth well allied with Heaven and Earth. The gods have found Agni the conspicuous one in the waters, in the work 3 of the sisters.

Geldner

Freude schuf der Weise von lauterem Wollen, durch seine Geburt der nahe Verwandte von Himmel und Erde. Sie fanden den sichtbaren im Wasser, die G├╢tter den Agni in der T├дtigkeit der Schwestern.

Grassmann

Und Lust empfand der weise, reingesinnte, verwandt der Erd’ und durch Geburt dem Himmel; Die G├╢tter fanden auf den sch├╢nen Agni in den Gew├дssern bei dem Werk der Schwestern.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe seven great rivers augmented in might the auspicious, pure, and radiant Agni as soon as he was born, in like manner as mares (tend) the newborn foal; the gods cherished the body (of Agni) at his birth.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The seven young women strengthened him of good fortune, who is white as he comes to birth, red in his greatness.
(Those) mares came to him (newly born) as to a new-born colt. The gods marveled at Agni at his birth.

Griffith

Him, Blessed One, the Seven strong Floods augmented, him white at birth and red when waxen mighty.
As mother mares run to their new-born you ling, so at his birth the Gods wondered at Agni.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬSpreading through the firmament with shining limbs, sanctifying the rite with intelligent and purifying (energies), and clothed with radiance, he bestows upon the worshiper abundant food and great and undiminished prosperity.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Stretching through the airy realm with his blazing limbs, purifying his resolve through the sage poets as his purifying filters,
clothing himself all around in flame, and being the life of the waters, he measures out his splendors, lofty and never wanting.

Griffith

Spreading with radiant limbs throughout the region, purging his power with wise purifications,
Robing himself in light, the life of waters, lie spreads abroad his high and perfect glories.

Oldenberg

Spreading with his bright limbs to the aerial space, purifying his power 1 by wise purifications, clothing himself in light, the life of the waters 2, he creates mighty, perfect beauty.

Mit seinen lichten Gliedern den Raum durchdringend, seinen Geist kl├дrend durch die Kl├дrungsmittel der Seher, in Glut sich kleidend und in der Wasser Lebenskraft, entfaltet er seine hohe, vollkommene Sch├╢nheit.

Grassmann

Mit lichten Gliedern dringend durch die L├╝fte, durch weises L├дutern seinen Sinn durchl├дuternd, In Licht gekleidet um die Flut der Wasser erlangt er grosse, ganz vollkomm’ne Sch├╢nheit.

Elizarenkova

рдЕрдирджрддреАрдГ рдЕрднрдХреНрд╖рдпрдиреНрддреАрдГ рдЕрджрдмреНрдзрд╛рдГ рдЕрд╣рд┐рдВрд╕рд┐рддрд╛рдГ рдорд╛рддреГрднреВрддрд╛рдГ рдЕрдкреЛрдЧреНрдирд┐рдГ рд╕реАрдВрд╕рд░реНрд╡рддреЛрд╡рд╡реНрд░рд╛рдЬ рд╡реНрд░рдЬрддрд┐ рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рд░рдкрд╛рдВрд╢реЛрд╖рдХрдГ рддрдЮреНрдЪрд╛рдкрдГ рд╢рдордпрдиреНрддрд┐рддрджреБрднрдпрдорд┐рд╣рдирд╛рд╕реНрддреАрддреНрдпреБрдХреНрддрдореНрднрд╡рддрд┐ рдХреАрджреГрд╢реНрдпрд╕реНрддрд╛рдГ рджрд┐рдпреЛрдпрд╣реНрд╡реАрдГ рдЕрдиреНрддрд░рд┐рдХреНрд╖рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдкрддреНрдпрднреВрддрд╛рдГ рдЕрд╡рд╕рд╛рдирд╛рдГ рд╡рд╕реНрддреНрд░рдордирд╛рдЪреНрдЫрд╛рджрдпрдиреНрддреНрдпрдГ рд╡рд╕реНрддреНрд░рд╕реНрдерд╛рдиреАрдпрд╕реНрдпрдЬрд▓рд╕реНрдп рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрдорд╛рдирддреНрд╡рд╛рддреН рдЕрддрдПрд╡рдирдЧреНрдирд╛рдГ рдХрд┐рдЮреНрдЪ рддрд╛рдЕрдкрд┐рд╕рдирд╛рдГ рд╕рдирд╛рддрдиреНрдпрдГ рдпреБрд╡рддрдпрдГ рдирд┐рддреНрдпрддрд░реБрдгреНрдпрдГ рдирд┐рддреНрдпрд╡реНрд░реБрджреНрдзрд╛рдЗрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ рд╕рдпреЛрдиреАрдГ рд╕рдорд╛рдирдордиреНрддрд░рд┐рдХреНрд╖рдВрдпреЛрдирд┐рд╕реНрдерд╛рдирдВрдпрд╛рд╕рд╛рдиреНрддрд╛рдГ рд╕рдкреНрддрд╡рд╛рдгреАрдГ рдирджреНрдпрдГ рдПрдХрдВ рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рдЩреНрдЧрд░реНрднрдЩреНрдЧрд░реНрднрд╕реНрдердВ рджрдзрд┐рд░реЗрджрдзрддреЗ тАМ рее рем рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬAgni everywhere repairs to the undevouring, undevoured (waters); the vast (offspring) of the firmament, not clothed, yet not naked, seven eternal ever youthfful rivers, sprung from the same source, received Agni as their common embryo.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Undevouring, undevoured waters: anadatir adabdh─Б, not extinguishing Agni, nor yet evaporated by him; not clothed: avas─Бn─Б anagn─Б, not wearing garments but invested by the water as by a robe

Jamison Brereton

He wandered toward them, who neither speak falsely nor can be deceived, who are the young women of heaven, neither clothing
themselves nor naked.
Here the young women of long ago, who came from the same womb, conceived their single embryoтАФthey, the seven voices.

Griffith

He sought heaven’s Mighty Ones, the unconsuming, the unimpaired, not clothed and yet not naked.
Then they, ancient and young, who dwell together, Seven sounding Rivers, as one germ received him.

Oldenberg

He has gone to (the waters) who do not eat, the undeceived ones, the young (daughters) of Heaven who are not clothed and (yet) are not naked. Here the former young (women) having the same origin, the seven sounds 1 have conceived one germ.

Geldner

Er ging in sie ein, die nicht essen und nicht Schaden leiden, in die j├╝ngsten T├╢chter des Himmels, die sich nicht kleiden und auch nicht nackt sind. Dort haben die Alten, die immer jugendlich sind, die einen gemeinsamen Scho├Я haben, den einen Keim empfangen, die sieben Stimmen.

Grassmann

Zu Himmels Str├╢men, treuen, die nicht zehren, die unbekleidet doch nicht nackt sind, schritt er; Dort nahmen auf den einen Spross die sieben Geschwisterstr├╢me, sie die alt doch jung sind.

Elizarenkova

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдЕрдм рд╕реНрддреНрд░реАрдкреБрд░реБрд╖реЛрдВ рдХреЗ рд╡рд┐рд╖рдп рдХреЛ рдЕрдЧрд▓реЗ рдордиреНрддреНрд░ рдореЗрдВ рдХрд╣рд╛ рд╣реИред

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╣реЗ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпреЛ ! рдЬреИрд╕реЗ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН (рд╕рдкреНрдд рд╡рд╛рдгреАрдГ) рд╕рд╛рдд рд╡рд╛рдгрд┐рдпреЛрдВ рдХреЛ (рд╕реАрдореН) рд╕рдм рдУрд░ рд╕реЗ (рд╡рд╡реНрд░рд╛рдЬ) рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реЛрддрд╛ рд╡реИрд╕реЗ (рдЕрддреНрд░) рдпрд╣рд╛рдБ (рдЕрдирджрддреАрдГ) рдЕрд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрдорд╛рди рдЕрд░реНрдерд╛рддреН рдЕрддреАрд╡ рд╕реВрдХреНрд╖реНрдо рдЬрд┐рдирдХреЗ рджрдиреНрдд (рдЕрджрдмреНрдзрд╛рдГ) рдЕрд╣рд┐рдВрд╕рдиреАрдп рдЕрд░реНрдерд╛рддреН рд╕рддреНрдХрд╛рд░ рдХрд░рдиреЗ рдпреЛрдЧреНрдп (рджрд┐рд╡рдГ) рджреЗрджреАрдкреНрдпрдорд╛рди (рдпрд╣реНрд╡реАрдГ) рдмрд╣реБрдд рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛ рдФрд░ рдЧреБрдг рд╕реНрд╡рднрд╛рд╡ рд╕реЗ рдпреБрдХреНрдд (рдЕрд╡рд╕рд╛рдирд╛рдГ) рд╕рдореАрдк рдореЗрдВ рдард╣рд░реА рд╣реБрдИ (рдЕрдирдЧреНрдиреАрдГ) рд╕рдм рдУрд░ рд╕реЗ рд╡рд╕реНрддреНрд░ рд╡рд╛ рдЖрднреВрд╖рдг рдЖрджрд┐ рд╕реЗ рдврдкреА рд╣реБрдИ (рд╕рдирд╛рдГ) рднреЛрдЧрдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реА (рд╕рдпреЛрдиреАрдГ) рд╕рдорд╛рди рдЬрд┐рди рдХреА рдпреЛрдирд┐ рдЕрд░реНрдерд╛рддреН рдПрдХ рдорд╛рддрд╛ рд╕реЗ рдЙрддреНрдкрдиреНрди рд╣реБрдИ рд╕рднреА рд╡реЗ (рдпреБрд╡рддрдпрдГ) рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рдпреМрд╡рдирд╛ рд╕реНрддреНрд░реА (рдПрдХрдореН) рдПрдХ рдЕрд░реНрдерд╛рддреН рдЕрд╕рд╣рд╛рдпрдХ (рдЧрд░реНрднрдореН) рдЧрд░реНрдн рдХреЛ (рджрдзрд┐рд░реЗ) рдзрд╛рд░рдг рдХрд░рддреАрдВ рд╡реЗрдВ рд╕реБрдЦреА рдХреНрдпреЛрдВ рди рд╣реЛрдВ? рееремрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЬреЛ рд╕рдорд╛рди рд░реВрдкрд╡рд╛рд▓реА рд╕реНрддреНрд░рд┐рдпрд╛рдБ рдЕрдкрдиреЗ-рдЕрдкрдиреЗ рд╕рдорд╛рди рдкрддрд┐рдпреЛрдВ рдХреЛ рдЕрдкрдиреА рдЗрдЪреНрдЫрд╛ рд╕реЗ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реЛрдХрд░ рдкрд░рд╕реНрдкрд░ рдкреНрд░реАрддрд┐ рдХреЗ рд╕рд╛рде рд╕рдиреНрддрд╛рдиреЛрдВ рдХреЛ рдЙрддреНрдкрдиреНрди рдХрд░ рдФрд░ рдЙрди рдХреА рд░рдХреНрд╖рд╛ рдХрд░ рдЙрдирдХреЛ рдЙрддреНрддрдо рд╢рд┐рдХреНрд╖рд╛ рджрд┐рд▓рд╛рддреА рд╣реИрдВ рд╡реЗ рд╕реБрдЦрдпреБрдХреНрдд рд╣реЛрддреА рд╣реИрдВред рдЬреИрд╕реЗ рдкрд░рд╛, рдкрд╢реНрдпрдиреНрддреА, рдордзреНрдпрдорд╛, рд╡реИрдЦрд░реА рдХрд░реНрдореНрдореЛрдкрд╛рд╕рдирд╛рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рди рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢ рдХрд░рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реА рддреАрдиреЛрдВ рдорд┐рд▓ рдХрд░ рдФрд░ рд╕рд╛рдд рд╡рд╛рдгреА рд╕рдм рд╡реНрдпрд╡рд╣рд╛рд░реЛрдВ рдХреЛ рд╕рд┐рджреНрдз рдХрд░рддреА рд╣реИрдВ, рд╡реИрд╕реЗ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рд╕реНрддреНрд░реА рдкреБрд░реБрд╖ рдзрд░реНрдореНрдо, рдЕрд░реНрде, рдХрд╛рдо рдФрд░ рдореЛрдХреНрд╖ рдХреЛ рд╕рд┐рджреНрдз рдХрд░ рд╕рдХрддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ рееремрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛ рдпрдерд╛ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рд╕рдкреНрдд рд╡рд╛рдгреАрдГ рд╕реАрдВ рд╡рд╡реНрд░рд╛рдЬ рддрдерд╛рд╜рддреНрд░рд╛рдирджрддреАрд░рджрдмреНрдзрд╛ рджрд┐рд╡реЛ рдпрд╣реНрд╡реАрд░рд╡рд╕рд╛рдирд╛ рдЕрдирдЧреНрдирд╛рд╕реНрд╕рдирд╛рдГ рд╕рдпреЛрдиреАрд░реНрдпреБрд╡рддрдп рдПрдХрдВ рдЧрд░реНрднрдВ рджрдзрд┐рд░реЗ рддрд╛рдГ рд╕реБрдЦрд┐рдиреНрдпрдГ рдХреБрддреЛ рди рд╕реНрдпреБрдГ? рееремрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдЕрде рд╕реНрддреНрд░реАрдкреБрд░реБрд╖рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдорд╛рд╣ред

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рд╡рд╡реНрд░рд╛рдЬ) рд╡реНрд░рдЬрддрд┐ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрддреЛрддрд┐ред рдЕрддреНрд░ рд╕рдВрд╣рд┐рддрд╛рдпрд╛рдорд┐рддрд┐ рджреАрд░реНрдШрдГред (рд╕реАрдореН) рд╕рд░реНрд╡рддрдГ (рдЕрдирджрддреАрдГ) рдЕрд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрдорд╛рдирд╛ рдЕрддреАрд╡ рд╕реВрдХреНрд╖реНрдорд╛ рджрдиреНрддрд╛ рдпрд╛рд╕рд╛рдиреНрддрд╛рдГ (рдЕрджрдмреНрдзрд╛рдГ) рдЕрд╣рд┐рдВрд╕рдиреАрдпрд╛рдГ рд╕рддреНрдХрд░реНрддреНрддрд╡реНрдпрд╛рдГ (рджрд┐рд╡рдГ) рджреЗрджреАрдкреНрдпрдорд╛рдирд╛рдГ (рдпрд╣реНрд╡реАрдГ) рдорд╣рд╛рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рдЧреБрдгрд╕реНрд╡рднрд╛рд╡рдпреБрдХреНрддрд╛рдГ (рдЕрд╡рд╕рд╛рдирд╛рдГ) рдЕрдиреНрддреЗ рд╕рдореАрдкреЗ рд╕реНрдерд┐рддрд╛рдГ (рдЕрдирдЧреНрдирд╛) рд╕рд░реНрд╡рддрд╛ рд╡рд╕реНрддреНрд░рднреВрд╖рдгрд╛рджрд┐рднрд┐рд░рд╛рдЪреНрдЫрд╛рджрд┐рддрд╛рдГ (рд╕рдирд╛рдГ) рднреЛрдХреНрддреНрд░реНрдпрдГ (рдЕрддреНрд░) (рдпреБрд╡рддрдпрдГ) рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрддрдпреМрд╡рдирд╛рдГ (рд╕рдпреЛрдиреАрдГ) рд╕рдорд╛рдирд╛ рдпреЛрдирд┐рд░реНрдпрд╛рд╕рд╛рдВ рддрд╛рдГ (рдПрдХрдореН) рдЕрд╕рд╣рд╛рдпрдореН (рдЧрд░реНрднрдореН) (рджрдзрд┐рд░реЗ) рдзрд░рдиреНрддрд┐ (рд╕рдкреНрдд) (рд╡рд╛рдгреАрдГ) рееремрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдпрджрд┐ рд╕рдорд╛рдирд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рд░реВрдкрд╕реНрд╡рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рдГ рд╕рдорд╛рдирд╛рдиреН рдкрддреАрдиреН рд╕реНрд╡реЗрдЪреНрдЫрдпрд╛ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдп рдкрд░рд╕реНрдкрд░рдкреНрд░реАрддреНрдпрд╛рддреН рд╕рдиреНрддрд╛рдирд╛рдиреБрддреНрдкрд╛рджреНрдп рд╕рдВрд░рдХреНрд╖реНрдп рд╕реБрд╢рд┐рдХреНрд╖рдпрдиреНрддрд┐ рддрд╛рдГ рд╕реБрдЦрдпреБрдХреНрддрд╛ рднрд╡рдиреНрддрд┐ рдпрдерд╛ рдкрд░рд╛ рдкрд╢реНрдпрдиреНрддреА рдордзреНрдпрдорд╛ рд╡реИрдЦрд░реА рдХрд░реНрдореНрдореЛрдкрд╛рд╕рдирд╛рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢рд┐рдХрд╛рд╕реНрддрд┐рд╕реНрддреНрд░рд╢реНрдЪ рдорд┐рд▓рд┐рддреНрд╡рд╛ рд╕рдкреНрдд рд╡рд╛рдгреНрдпрдГ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╛рдиреНрд╡реНрдпрд╡рд╣рд╛рд░рд╛рдиреН рд╕рд╛рдзрдпрдиреНрддрд┐ рддрдерд╛ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдВрд╕рдГ рд╕реНрддреНрд░реАрдкреБрд░реБрд╖рд╛ рдзрд░реНрдорд╛рд░реНрдердХрд╛рдордореЛрдХреНрд╖рд╛рдиреН рд╕рд╛рджреНрдзреБрдВ рд╢рдХреНрдиреБрд╡рдиреНрддрд┐ рееремрее

рд╕рд╛рдпрдг-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрдореН

рдШреГрддрд╕реНрдпреЛрджрдХрд╕реНрдп рдпреЛрдиреМрд╕реНрдерд╛рдиреЗ рдЕрдиреНрддрд░рд┐рдХреНрд╖реЗ рд╕рдВрд╣рддрдГ рдкреБрдЮреНрдЪреАрднреВрддрд╛рдГ рд╣рдиреНрддреЗрдГрдХреНрд╡рд┐рдкреН рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд░реВрдкрд╛рдГ рдирд╛рдирд╛рд░реВрдкрд╛рдГ рд╕реНрддреАрд░реНрдгрд╛рдГ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рддреНрд░рдкреНрд░рд╕реГрддрд╛рдГ рдЕрд╕реНрдпрд╛рдЧреНрдиреЗрдГрд░рд╢реНрдордпрдГ рдордзреВрдирд╛рдореБрджрдХрд╛рдирд╛рдВ рд╕реНрд░рд╡рдереЗрд╕реНрд░рд╡рдгреЗ рдирд┐рдорд┐рддреНрддреЗ рдЕрд╕реНрдереБрд╕реНрддрд┐рд╖реНрдардиреНрддрд┐ рдкрд┐рдиреНрд╡ рдорд╛рдирд╛рдГ рдкреВрд░реНрдпрдорд╛рдгрд╛рдГ рдЕрддреНрд░рдЕрдЧреНрдиреМрдЖрдкрдГ рдзреЗрдирд╡рдГ рд╕рд░реНрд╡реЗрд╖рд╛рдВ рдкреНрд░реАрдгрдпрд┐рддреНрд░реНрдпрдГ рдЕрднрд╡рдиреН рд╕рдореАрдЪреА рд╕рдордЮреНрдЪрддреНрдпреМ рд╢реЛрднрдорд╛рдиреЗ рдорд╣реА рдорд╣рддреНрдпреМрджреНрдпрд╛рд╡рд╛рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реНрдпреМ рджрд╕реНрдорд╕реНрдпрджрд░реНрд╢рдиреАрдпрд╕реНрдпрд╛рдЧреНрдиреЗрд░реНрдорд╛рддрд░рд╛ рдорд╛рддрд░реМ рднрд╡рддрдГ рее рен рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬAggregated in the womb of the waters, (his rays) spread abroad; and omniform, are here effective for the diffusion of the sweet (Soma), like kine full uddered; the mighty (Heaven and Earth) are the fitting parents of the graceful Agni.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The womb of the waters: the antarikс╣гa, mid-heaven, or the firmament, the region of vapour

Jamison Brereton

Strewn about and pressing together are his (flames) of all colors in the womb of ghee and in the stream of the honeyed (soma juices).
Here have the swelling cows [=milk offerings] taken their stand. The two mothers of wondrous (Agni) [=the two fire churning sticks?] are the two great ones, the two united.

Griffith

His piles, assuming every form, are scattered where flow sweet waters, at the spring of fatness;
There stood the milch-kine with full-laden udders, and both paired Mighty Mothers of the Wondrous.

Oldenberg

His compact masses assuming every shape are spread in the womb of ghee, in the streaming of honey. There the swelling milch-cows have stationed themselves. Great are the parents of the wonderfully mighty (Agni) who are turned towards each other 1.

Geldner

Ausgebreitet sind seine zusammengefalteten Glieder, die bunten im Scho├Яe des Schmalzes, im Strome der S├╝├Яigkeiten. Dort standen die milchstrotzenden K├╝he. Die M├╝tter des Meisters sind das gro├Яe Paar Himmel und Erde.

Grassmann

Die vielgestalt’gen Schichten sind gelegt ihm, im Schoss der Butter, in dem Strom der Tr├дnke; Dort standen schon von Milch geschwellt die K├╝he, vereint des wunderkr├дft’gen grosse Aeltern.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬSon of strength, sustained by all, you shine, possessing bright and rapid rays; when the vigorous Agni is magnified by praise, then the showers of sweet rain descend.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Being carried (as an embryo), o son of strength, you have flashed out, assuming your wondrous forms that blaze and rage.
Streams of honey and ghee drip where the bull has grown strong
through our poetic craft.

Griffith

Carefully cherished, Son of Strength, thou shoncst assuming lasting and refulgent beauties.
Full streams of fatness and sweet juice descended, there where the Mighty One grew strong by wisdom.

Oldenberg

Having been carried (in the waters) thou hast shone forth, O son of strength, assuming wonderful shapes brilliant and fierce. The streams of honey and ghee drip, where the male has grown by wisdom.

Grassmann

Gen├дhrt erstrahltest weit, o Sohn der Kraft, du, annehmend lichte, gl├дnzende Gestalten; Der s├╝ssen Butter Str├╢me tr├дufeln nieder dort, wo der Stier durch Seherkraft erstarkt ist.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬAt his birth he knew the udder of his parent and let forth its torrents, and its speech (of thunder); there was no one to detect him, lurking in the deep, with his auspicious associates, (the winds), and the many (waters) of the firmament.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Knew the udder of his parent: pitur┼лdhan viveda: the parent here is the firmament, and the udder the clouds, or the accusative ulated stores of rain

Jamison Brereton

At his birth, he found the udder even of his father. He let loose its streams and spurts in every direction.
Him who moves in hiding from his kind companions [=the priests]тАФ (though) he was not hidden from the young women of heavenтАФ

Griffith

From birth he knew even his Father’s bosom, he set his voices and his streams in motion;
Knew him who moved with blessed Friends in secret, with the young Dames of heaven. He stayed not hidden.

Oldenberg

By (his) nature he has found his father’s udder 1; he has sent forth his streams and his showers 2. Walking 3 hidden to his dear friends he has not been hidden to the young (daughters) of Heaven 4.

Geldner

Er fand gleich bei seiner Geburt des Vaters Euter; er entfesselte dessen Strahlen, dessen Stimmen. Ihn, der vor seinen guten Freunden sich verborgen hielt - vor den j├╝ngsten T├╢chtern des Himmels war er nicht verborgen.

Grassmann

Des Vaters Busen fand durch eigne Kraft er, und seine Str├╢me goss er aus und Tr├дnke, Fand den, der heimlich ging mit holden Freunden; nicht war er selbst versteckt in Himmels Str├╢men.

Elizarenkova

рдЕрдпрдордЧреНрдирд┐рдГ рдкрд┐рддреБрд╢реНрдЪ рдЕрдиреНрддрд░рд┐рдХреНрд╖рд╕реНрдпрдЧрд░реНрднрдВ рд╡реГрд╖реНрдЯрд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рд░рд╛рдЧрд░реНрднрднреВрддрдВ рдЬрдирд┐рддреБрдГ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╕реНрдпрд▓реЛрдХрд╕реНрдпрдЬрдирдпрд┐рддреБрд╢реНрдЪ рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдо рдгрд╢реНрдЪ рд▓реЛрдХрдВ рдмрднреНрд░реЗрдмрд┐рднрд░реНрддрд┐ рдПрдХрдПрд╡рд╛рдЧреНрдирд┐рдГ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡реАрд░реНрдмрд╣реНрд╡реЛрдГ рдкреАрдкреНрдпрд╛рдирд╛рдГ рдкреНрдпрд╛рдпрдорд╛рдирд╛рдГ рд╡реГрджреНрдзрд┐рдореНрдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрддрд╛рдГ рдУрд╖рдзреАрдГ рдЕрдзрдпрдд рдзрдпрддрд┐рднрдХреНрд╖рдпрддрд┐ рд╕рдкрддреНрдиреА рд╕рдорд╛рдирдПрдХрдГ рд╕реВрд░реНрдпрдГрдкрддрд┐рд░реНрдпрдпреЛрдГрддреЗ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпреЗ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпреЗрднреНрдпреЛрд╣рд┐рддреЗ рдЙрднреЗрджреНрдпрд╛- рд╡рд╛рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реНрдпреМ рд╡реГрд╖реНрдгреЗрд╡рд░реНрд╖рд┐рддреНрд░реЗ рдЕрд╕реНрдореИрд╢реБрдЪреНрдпреЗрдЕрдЧреНрдирдпреЗ рд╕рдмрдиреНрдзреВрднрд╡рддрдГ рдЕрдирдпреЛрдГ рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рд░реЗрд╡рдмрдиреНрдзреБрд░рд┐рддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ рд╣реЗ рдЕрдЧреНрдиреЗ рддреНрд╡рдВ- рддреЗрджреНрдпрд╛рд╡рд╛рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реНрдпреМ рдирд┐рдкрд╛рд╣рд┐ рдирд┐рддрд░рд╛рдВрд░рдХреНрд╖ рее резреж рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬHe cherishes the embryo of the parent (firmament), and of the genitive rator (of the world); he alone consumes many flourishing (plural nts); the associated brides (of the Sun, Heaven and Earth), who are kind to man, are both of kin to that pure showerer (of blessings); do you, Agni, ever preserve them.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

(Him) who was the embryo of his father and begetter did he himself carry. Alone, he suckled upon the many swelling females.
(Protect) his two kindred cowives for the blazing bull, protect the pair [=the fire-churning sticks?] belonging to the sons of Manu for him.

Griffith

He nursed the Infant of the Sire and Maker: alone the Babe sucked many a teeming bosom.
Guard, for the Bright and Strong, the fellow-spouses friendly to men and bound to him in kinship.

Oldenberg

He bore (in his womb) the germ of the sire, of the father who begat him 1. He, being one, sucked many (nurses) rich in milk 2. Observe for this manly, bright one the two wives bound in kinship, belonging to men 3.

Geldner

Er trug die Leibesfrucht des Vaters und Erzeugers; er als einziger saugte an vielen Milchstrotzenden. Die beiden Verwandten Himmel und Erde sind dem reinen Bullen seine gemeinsamen Frauen. Gib acht auf seine beiden menschlichen Frauen!

Grassmann

Des Vaters und Erzeugers Spross ern├дhrt’ er; er sog allein an vieler M├╝tter Br├╝sten; Die beiden, die dem lichten Stier verwandt sind und ihm verm├дhlt, die menschenholden, hege.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe great Agni increases on the broad unbounded (firmament), for the waters supply abundant nutriment, and plural cid, he sleeps in the birth-plural ce of the waters for the service of the sister streams.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The great one has grown strong in the broad and unrestricted (place). The waters (go) to Agni, for glory gets the girls.
In the womb of truth lay the lord of the house, Agni, within the work of the kindred sisters.

Griffith

The Mighty One increased in space unbounded; full many a glorious flood gave strength to Agni.
Friend of the house, within the lap of Order lay Agni, in the Sister Rivers’ service.

Oldenberg

The great one has grown up in the wide unbounded space 1. The Waters (have made) Agni (grow): for many glorious ones 2 (have come) together 3. He lay in the womb of Rita, the domestic (god) Agni, in the work 4 of the uterine sisters.

Der Gro├Яe ist im weiten unbeengten Raum aufgewachsen; die Wasser zogen den Agni gro├Я, denn ein Geehrter hat viele Frauen beisammen. Im Scho├Яe der Wahrheit ruhte der Hausgebieter, Agni inmitten der T├дtigkeit der verwandten Schwestern.

Grassmann

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe invincible Agni, the cherisher of the valiant in battle, the seen of all, shining by his own lustre, the genitive rator (of the world), the embryo of the waters, the chief of leaders, the mighty, is he who has begotton the waters for (the benefit of) the offerer of the libation.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Like a burden-bearing foal [?], at the meeting place of the great (waters?), the one desirable for a son to see and foaming with radiance,
the begetter who gave birth to the ruddy (cows of dawn), the embryo of the waters, and the best of men is the young Agni.

Griffith

As keen supporter where great waters gather, light-shedder whom the brood rejoice to look on;
He who begat, and will beget, the dawnlights, most manly, Child of Floods, is youthful Agni.

Oldenberg

Like a horse that carries (the prize), in the assembly of the great (waters) 1, visible to his son 2, he whose тАж is light 3: he who as father begat the ruddy cows 4, he the son of the waters is the most manly, restless 5 Agni.

Geldner

Wie ein tragender Elefant im Zusammenflu├Я der Hochwasser, ein begehrter Anblick f├╝r den Sohn, glanzversch├╢nt, er der als Erzeuger die K├╝he hervorgebracht hat, das Kind der Gew├дsser, der mannhafteste, der j├╝ngste Agni.

Grassmann

Als Strebepfeiler in der Wellen Andrang ist sehenswerth dem Sohn der lichtdurchstrahlte; Er, der das Licht erzeugte als Erzeuger, der Wasser Spross, der starke, rasche Agni.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬThe auspicious timber has genitive rated the graceful and multiform embryo of the waters and the plural nts; the gods approached him with reverence, and worshipped the adorable and mighty (Agni) as soon as born.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The (fire-churning) WoodтАФshe who brings good fortuneтАФhas given birth to the lovely embryo of the waters and of the plants, to him of various colors.
Since they have united in their thinking, even the gods befriend the
most admired and powerful one as soon as he is born.

Griffith

Him, varied in his form, the lovely Infant of floods and plants the blessed wood hath gendered.
Gods even, moved in spirit, came around him, and served him at his birth, the Strong, the Wondrous.

Oldenberg

To him, the glorious son of the waters and of the plants, the blessed wood 1 has given birth, in his many shapes. Even the gods, for they agreed in their mind, honoured him who had been born the most wonderful and strong.

Geldner

Das gerngesehene Kind der Wasser, der Pflanzen hat in ver├дnderter Gestalt das holde Reibholz geboren. Auch die G├╢tter waren ja damit einverstanden; sie bevorzugten den hochgesch├дtzten, starken, als er geboren war.

Grassmann

Den sch├╢nen Spross der Wasser und Gew├дchse, an Farben bunt gebar die holde Vana; Die G├╢tter selbst, sie kamen hin mit Freuden, bewunderten das pr├дcht’ge Kind, das starke.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMighty sins, like brilliant lightning, associate with the self-shining Agni, great in his own abode, as if in a (deep) cavern, as they milk forth ambrosia into the boundless and vast ocean.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Like blazing flashes of lightning, lofty radiant beams accompany Agni, foaming with radiance,
as they yield as their milk the immortal (Agni), grown strong within his own seat as if in hiding, within the unbounded container.

Griffith

Like brilliant lightnings, mighty luminaries accompany the light-diffusing Agni,
Waxen, as ’twere in secret, in his dwelling, while in the boundless stall they milk out Amrta.

Oldenberg

Mighty rays of light like brilliant lightnings, milking (the sap of) immortality in the boundless stable, accompanied Agni whose тАж is light 1, who had grown up in his own house, as it were in secret.

Geldner

Hohe Strahlen begleiten den glanzversch├╢nten Agni wie die hellen Blitze den Regen. Ihm, der gleichsam heimlich in seiner Heimat gro├Я geworden war im unerme├Яlichen Ozean, stehen die den G├╢ttertrank milchenden K├╝he zur Seite.

Grassmann

Dem lichtdurchstrahlten strebten lichte G├╢tter, dem Agni zu wie glanzbegabte Blitze, Aus ihm, der heimlich wuchs in seinem Sitze, im weiten Raum den G├╢ttertrank sich melkend.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬI, the instrumental tutor of the rite, worship you with oblations; desirous of your favour, I implore your friendship; grant, along with the gods, protection to him who praises you, preserve us with your well-regulated rays.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

I call upon you, sacrificing with my offerings, and I call upon your companionship and your favor with desire.
With the gods, give help in full measure to the singer, and guard us with your faces that belong to the house.

Griffith

I sacrificing serve thee with oblations and crave with longing thy good-will and friendship.
Grant, with the Gods, thy grace to him who lauds thee, protect us with thy rays that guard the homestead.

Oldenberg

I magnify thee, worshipping thee with offerings; I magnify (thee) desirous of thy friendship, of thy favour. Together with the gods give help to him who praises thee, and protect us with thy domestic faces.

Geldner

Und ich rufe dich als Opfernder mit Spenden an; ich rufe deine Freundschaft und Huld aus Zuneigung an. Mit den G├╢ttern erweise dem S├дnger Gnade und beh├╝te uns mit deinen h├дuslichen Erscheinungsformen!

Grassmann

Auch ich der Opfrer ehre dich mit Opfern, erfleh begierig deine Huld und Freundschaft; Miss zu dem S├дnger Labung durch die G├╢tter und sch├╝tze uns durch h├дusliches Ergl├дnzen.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬApproaching you, benevolent Agni, and performing all holy acts that are the cause of opulence, offering oblations with earnestness and in abundance, may we overcome the hostile hosts that are without gods.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

May we overcome the hostile: abhiс╣гy─Бma pс╣Ыtan─Бy┼лr adev─Бn;or, it may mean, may we overcome the hosts of those who are not gods, i.e. the r─Бkс╣гasas, or evil spirits, obstructing sacrifices

Jamison Brereton

As your dependents, o well-guiding Agni, receiving all riches
and thrusting ourselves forward with a fame that comes with good
seed, we would prevail over the godless battle-mongers.

Griffith

May we, O Agni, thou who leadest wisely, thy followers and masters of all treasures,
Strong in the glory of our noble offspring, subdue the godless when they seek the battle.

Oldenberg

As thy followers, O Agni, best leader, winning all precious (treasures), pressing onward with fertile glory, may we overcome the godless who seek to combat us.

Geldner

Als deine Hausgenossen, du guter F├╝hrer Agni, alle Gl├╝cksg├╝ter empfangend, durch den Ruhm eines guten Samens uns fortpflanzend wollen wir die feindseligen Gottlosen bestehen.

Grassmann

Uns, deine Treuen, der du trefflich leitest, lass, Agni, aller G├╝ter F├╝ll’ empfangen, Durch kinderreichen Segen vorw├дrts dringen, die gottvergessnen Feinde uns besiegen.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYou, Agni, are the commendable announcer of the gods, cognizant of all sacred rites; plural cid, you abide among mortals, and, like a charioteer, you follow the gods, accomplishing (their wishes).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Here have you come to be the beacon of the gods, o Agni, delighting and knowing all poetic crafts.
As the lord of the household, you allowed mortals to settle down, and as a charioteer bringing success, you journey following the gods.

Griffith

Ensign of Gods hast thou become, O Agni, joy-giver, knower of all secret wisdom.
Friend of the homestead, thou hast lightened mortals: carborne thou goest to the Gods, fulfilling.

Oldenberg

Thou hast been here as the banner of the gods, Agni, joy-giving, knowing all wisdom. As the domestic (god) thou hast harboured the mortals. As the charioteer thou goest along straightway after the gods.

Geldner

Du Agni wardst zum Feldzeichen der G├╢tter, du der Wohlredende, der alle Weisheiten kennt. Du gabst als Hausherr allen Sterblichen Wohnung; du suchst als Wagenfahrer die G├╢tter erfolgreich auf.

Grassmann

Du Agni warst der G├╢tter helles Banner, erfreuend, kennend alle Geisteskr├дfte; Du siedeltest die Menschen an als Hausfreund; im Wagen f├дhrest stracks du zu den G├╢ttern.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬCome to us with friendly, auspicious, and mighty aids, you who are great and all-pervading; besto wupon us ample riches, safe from injury, well-spoken of, desirable, and renowned.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Come to us together with your kind companionship, hastening as the great one together with your great help.
Make for us abundant wealth that brings us safely across, and a share for us that brings beautiful speech and glory.

Griffith

Come unto us with thine auspicious friendship, come speeding, Mighty, with thy mighty succours.
Grant us abundant wealth that saves from danger, that brings a good repute, a glorious portion.

Oldenberg

1 Come to us with thy gracious friendship, speeding, great, with thy great blessings. Bestow on us plentiful victorious wealth; make our share glorious and adorned with fine speech.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬI address to you, Agni, who are of old, these eternal as well as recent adorations; these solemn sacrifices are offered to the showerer of benefits, who in every birth is established (among men), cognizant of all that exists.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

These your births of long ago, o Agni, and your present ones I shall proclaim for the ancient one.
Great soma-pressings for the bull have been made here. J─Бtavedas has been installed in one birth after another.

Griffith

To thee who art of old these songs, O Agni, have I declared, the ancient and the later.
These great libations to the Strong are offiered: in every birth is Jatavedas stablished.

Oldenberg

These old births of thine, O Agni, and the recent ones I have told forth to thee the ancient one. These great libations (of Soma) have been prepared for the manly one; generation by generation G├вtavedas has been placed (on the altar).

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe undecaying J─Бtavedas, who in every birth is established (among men), is kindled by the Vi┼Ыv─Бmitras; may we, (enjoying) his favour, ever be (held) in the auspicious good-will of that adorable (deity).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Having been installed in one birth after another, J─Бtavedas, the
inexhaustible, is kindled by the Vi┼Ыv─Бmitras.
We would be within the good will of him who is worthy of the sacrifice, even within his favorable benevolence.

Griffith

Stablished in every birth is Jatavedas, kindled perpetual by the Visvamitras.
May we rest ever in the loving-kindness, in the auspicious grace of him the Holy.

Oldenberg

G├вtavedas, placed (on the altar) generation after generation, is kindled by the Visv├вmitras, the indefatigable (or everlasting). May we dwell in the grace of him the worshipful, yea, in his blissful kindness.

Von Geschlecht zu Geschlecht eingesetzt wird der nie ermattende Jatavedas von den Visvamitra┬┤s entflammt. An dieses Opferw├╝rdigen Gunst, an seinem gl├╝ckbringenden Wohlwollen m├╢chten wir teilhaben.

Grassmann

In jedem Haus ist Gast der Wesenkenner, ohn’ End’ entflammt vom Stamm des Vi├зvamitra; In seiner Gunst, des hehren, seien stets wir theilhaftig hohen, segensreichen Gl├╝ckes.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬPowerful Agni, (fulfiller) of good works, convey, rejoicing this our sacrifice towards the gods; invoker of the gods, bestow upon us abundant food; grant us, Agni, great wealth.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

O you endowed with strength, you of strong resolve, place this sacrifice among the gods for us, giving (it to them).
Hold forth the lofty refreshing drinks for us, o Hotar. O Agni, win great wealth by sacrifice.

Griffith

This sacrifice of ours do thou, O Mighty, O truly Wise, bear to the Gods rejoicing.
Grant us abundant food, thou priestly Herald, vouchsafe to give us ample wealth, O Agni.

Oldenberg

Bring thou, O strong one, this sacrifice of ours to the gods, O wise one, as a liberal giver. Bestow on us, O Hotri, abundant food; Agni, obtain by sacrificing mighty wealth for us.

Geldner

Grassmann

Dies Opfer schaffe du, o kraftbegabter, uns g├╢tterw├дrts, o wirkungsreicher, freundlich; O Priester, schenk uns reiche Labetr├дnke, und grossen Schatz, o Agni, opfre her uns.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬGrant, Agni, to the offerer of the oblation, the earth, the bestower of cattle, the means of many (pious rites), such that it may be perpetual; may there be to us sons and grandsons born in our race, and may your good-will ever be upon us.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

This hymn is the refrain of several subsequent s┼лktas; this hymn also occurs in the S─Бmaveda

Jamison Brereton

тАУ Make the milk-libation, the very wondrous winning of the cow, succeed, o Agni, for him who invokes you most constantly.
There should be for us a son and a lineage that proliferates. Agni, let this your favor be for us.

Griffith

As holy food, Agni, to thine’invoker give wealth in cattle, lasting, rich in marvels.
To us he born a son, and spreading offspring. Agni, be this thy gracious will to us-ward.

Oldenberg

Procure, O Agni, for ever, to him who implores thee, (the gift of) nourishment 1, the wonderful acquiring of the cow. May a son be ours, offspring that continues our race. Agni, may this favour of thine abide with us!

Geldner

Erziel, o Agni, Segen, den vielwirkenden Lohn einer Kuh f├╝r den am h├дufigsten rufenden S├дnger! Ein leiblicher Sohn, der das Geschlecht fortpflanzt, soll uns werden. Agni, diese Gnade von dir soll uns zuteil werden!

Grassmann

Dem Beter schaff als Labung wunderreichen Besitz an Rindern fort und fort, o Agni, Ein eigner Sohn sei uns und Stammvermehrung, das sei uns, Agni, deine Gunsterweisung.

Elizarenkova

рдкреБрдирд╕реНрддрдореЗрд╡ рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдорд╛рд╣ред

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдЗрд│рд╛рдореН) рд╕реНрддреБрддреНрдпрд╛рдВ рд╡рд╛рдЪрдореН (рдЕрдЧреНрдиреЗ) рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рдиреН (рдкреБрд░реБрджрдВрд╕рдореН) рдкреБрд░реВрдгрд┐ рджрдВрд╕рд╛рдВрд╕рд┐ рдХрд░реНрдорд╛рдгрд┐ рднрд╡рдиреНрддрд┐ рдпрд╕реНрдпрд╛рд╕реНрддрд╛рдореН (рд╕рдирд┐рдореН) рд╡рд┐рднрдХреНрддрд╛рдореН (рдЧреЛрдГ) рд╡рд╛рдЪрдГ (рд╢рд╢реНрд╡рддреНрддрдордореН) рдЕрдирд╛рджрд┐рднреВрддрдВ рд╢рдмреНрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╕рдореНрдмрдиреНрдзрдореН (рд╣рд╡рдорд╛рдирд╛рдп) рдЖрдирдиреНрджрд╛рдп (рд╕рд╛рдз) рд╕рд╛рдзреНрдиреБрд╣рд┐ред рдЕрддреНрд░ рд╡рд┐рдХрд░рдгрд╡реНрдпрддреНрдпрдпреЗрди рд╢рдкреНред (рд╕реНрдпрд╛рддреН) (рдирдГ) рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдХрдореН (рд╕реВрдиреБрдГ) рдкреБрддреНрд░рдГ (рддрдирдпрдГ) рд╡рд┐рд╕реНрддреАрд░реНрдгрдмреБрджреНрдзрд┐рдГ (рд╡рд┐рдЬрд╛рд╡рд╛) рд╡рд┐рд╢реЗрд╖рдг рдкреНрд░рд╛рджреБрд░реНрднреВрддрдГ (рдЕрдЧреНрдиреЗ) рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рдиреН (рд╕рд╛) (рддреЗ) (рд╕реБрдорддрд┐рдГ) рдЙрддреНрддрдорд╛ рдкреНрд░рдЬреНрдЮрд╛ (рднреВрддреБ) рднрд╡рддреБ (рдЕрд╕реНрдореЗ) рдЕрд╕реНрдорднреНрдпрдореН реереирейрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╡рд┐рджреБрд╖рд╛рдорд┐рдпрдореЗрд╡ рдпреЛрдЧреНрдпрддрд╛рд╕реНрддрд┐ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╛рдиреНрдХреБрдорд╛рд░рд╛рдиреН рдХреБрдорд╛рд░реАрд╢реНрдЪ рд╡рд┐рджреБрд╖реАрдГ рд╕рдВрдкрд╛рджрдпреЗрддреН рдпрддрдГ рд╕рд░реНрд╡реЗ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рдпрд╛рдГ рдлрд▓рдВ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдп рд╕реБрдорддрдпрдГ рд╕реНрдпреБрд░рд┐рддрд┐ реереирейрее рдЕрддреНрд░ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рддреНрд╕реНрддреНрд░реАрдкреБрд░реБрд╖рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рдЬрдиреНрдордкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕рд╛рдХрд░рдгрд╛рджреЗрддрджрд░реНрдерд╕реНрдп рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдереЗрди рд╕рд╣ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐рд░реНрд╡реЗрджреНрдпрд╛ рее рдЗрддрд┐ рддреГрддреАрдпрдордгреНрдбрд▓реЗ рдкреНрд░рдердордВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рд╖реЛрдбрд╢реЛ рд╡рд░реНрдЧрд╢реНрдЪ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрддрдГ рее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдирд╛рдВрдиреА рд╕рд░реНрд╡ рдХреБрдорд╛рд░ рд╡ рдХреБрдорд╛рд░реАрдВрдирд╛ рдкрдВрдбрд┐рдд рд╡ рдкрдВрдбрд┐рддрд╛ рдмрдирд╡рд╛рд╡реЗ. рдЬреНрдпрд╛рдореБрд│реЗ рд╕рд░реНрд╡ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпреЗрдЪреЗ рдлрд│ рдорд┐рд│реВрди рд╕реБрдорддреА рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рд╡реНрд╣рд╛рд╡реА. рее реирей рее
